      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse">About P.G. Wodehouse</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1198684105p3/7963.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/7963.P_G_Wodehouse">P.G. Wodehouse
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
5,399
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15180027696869526960">Sir Pelham Grenville Wodehouse, KBE, was a comic writer who enjoyed enormous popular success during a career of more than seventy years and continues to be widely read over 40 years after his death. Despite the political and social upheavals that occurred during his life, much of which was spent in France and the United States, Wodehouse's main canvas remained that of prewar English upper-class so</span>
  <span id="freeText15180027696869526960" style="display:none">Sir Pelham Grenville Wodehouse, KBE, was a comic writer who enjoyed enormous popular success during a career of more than seventy years and continues to be widely read over 40 years after his death. Despite the political and social upheavals that occurred during his life, much of which was spent in France and the United States, Wodehouse's main canvas remained that of prewar English upper-class society, reflecting his birth, education, and youthful writing career.<br /><br />An acknowledged master of English prose, Wodehouse has been admired both by contemporaries such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4025.Hilaire_Belloc" title="Hilaire Belloc" rel="nofollow noopener">Hilaire Belloc</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11315.Evelyn_Waugh" title="Evelyn Waugh" rel="nofollow noopener">Evelyn Waugh</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6989.Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling" rel="nofollow noopener">Rudyard Kipling</a> and by more recent writers such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams" title="Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">Douglas Adams</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3299.Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie" rel="nofollow noopener">Salman Rushdie</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" title="Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Pratchett</a>. Sean O'Casey famously called him "English literature's performing flea", a description that Wodehouse used as the title of a collection of his letters to a friend, Bill Townend.<br /><br />Best known today for the <i>Jeeves</i> and <i>Blandings Castle</i> novels and short stories, Wodehouse was also a talented playwright and lyricist who was part author and writer of fifteen plays and of 250 lyrics for some thirty musical comedies. He worked with Cole Porter on the musical <i>Anything Goes</i> (1934) and frequently collaborated with Jerome Kern and Guy Bolton. He wrote the lyrics for the hit song <i>Bill</i> in Kern's Show Boat (1927), wrote the lyrics for the Gershwin/Romberg musical <i>Rosalie</i> (1928), and collaborated with Rudolf Friml on a musical version of <i>The Three Musketeers</i> (1928).</span>
  <a data-text-id="15180027696869526960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

In his absence he has allowed Jeeves to offer his services to William &quot;Bill&quot; Rowcester, the impoverished 9th Earl of Rowcester, whose stately home, Rowcester Abbey, is an encumbrance for which the Earl is seeking a buyer.
